</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Legislature</th><td><a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Legislative Assembly of the Cayman Islands">Legislative Assembly</a></td></tr><tr style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Water&#160;(%)</div></th><td>1.6</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Highest&#160;elevation<div href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>&#32;(<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">192nd</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedbottomrow"><th href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>&#32;(<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">11th</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>&#160;<span style="font-weight:normal;">(nominal)</span></th><td>2014<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>&#160;estimate</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Total</div></th><td>$3.480 billion<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unstats1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unstats1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>&#32;(<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">160th</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedbottomrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Per capita</div></th><td>$58,808<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unstats1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unstats1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>&#32;(<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">9th</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">HDI</a>&#160;<span style="font-weight:normal;">(2013)</span></th><td>0.888<br /><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="color:darkgreen">very high</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Currency</th><td><a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands_dollar" title="Cayman Islands dollar">Cayman Islands dollar</a> (<a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">KYD</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">Time zone</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/UTC-5:00" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC-5:00">UTC-5:00</a> (<a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">EST</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Postcodes_in_the_United_Kingdom#British_Overseas_Territories" title="Postcodes in the United Kingdom">UK postcode</a></th><td class="adr"><div class="postal-code">KYx-xxxx</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Date format</th><td>dd/mm/yyyy</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand traffic">Driving side</a></th><td>left</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Calling code</th><td><a href="/wiki/North_American_Numbering_Plan" title="North American Numbering Plan">+1</a>-<a href="/wiki/Area_code_345" title="Area code 345">345</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:KY" title="ISO 3166-2:KY">KY</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.ky" title=".ky">.ky</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Cayman Islands</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ən/: &#39;on&#39; in &#39;button&#39;">ən</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>) are an autonomous <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territories" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territories">British Overseas Territory</a> in the western <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. The 264-square-kilometre (102-square-mile) territory comprises the three islands of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Cayman" title="Grand Cayman">Grand Cayman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Brac" title="Cayman Brac">Cayman Brac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Cayman" title="Little Cayman">Little Cayman</a>, which are located to the south of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and northeast of <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán Peninsula</a>. As of spring 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the population of the Cayman Islands was estimated to be 64,420 making it the second-most populated British overseas territory after <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eso_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eso-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The capital city is <a href="/wiki/George_Town,_Cayman_Islands" title="George Town, Cayman Islands">George Town</a>, situated on Grand Cayman, by far the most populous of the three islands.
</p><p>The Cayman Islands is considered to be part of the geographic <a href="/wiki/Western_Caribbean_Zone" title="Western Caribbean Zone">Western Caribbean Zone</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a>. The territory is often considered a major world <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">offshore financial haven</a> for international businesses and many wealthy individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="History of the Cayman Islands">History of the Cayman Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Jamaica" title="Colony of Jamaica">Colony of Jamaica</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a></div>
<p>No archaeological evidence for an indigenous presence has been found on the Cayman Islands<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and it is therefore thought that they were discovered by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> on 10 May 1503 on his final voyage to the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Cayman_Islands_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Cayman_Islands-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He named 'Las Tortugas' due to the large number of turtles on the islands (which were soon hunted to near-extinction),<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Cayman_Islands_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Cayman_Islands-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> however in the succeeding decades the islands began to be referred to as the Caymans, after the <a href="/wiki/Caiman" title="Caiman">caimans</a> present there.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Cayman_Islands_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Cayman_Islands-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> No immediate colonisation occurred following Columbus's discovery, however a variety of settlers from various backgrounds made their home on the islands, including <a href="/wiki/Pirate" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirate">pirates</a>, shipwrecked sailors, and deserters from <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a>'s army in <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a> briefly visited the islands in 1586.<sup id="cite_ref-keytocayman.com_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-keytocayman.com-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cayman_Islands_National_Museum_-_George_Town,_Grand_Cayman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Cayman_Islands_National_Museum_-_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg/220px-Cayman_Islands_National_Museum_-_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Cayman_Islands_National_Museum_-_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg/330px-Cayman_Islands_National_Museum_-_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Cayman_Islands_National_Museum_-_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg/440px-Cayman_Islands_National_Museum_-_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2728" data-file-height="1926" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cayman_Islands_National_Museum_-_George_Town,_Grand_Cayman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cayman Islands National Museum, George Town, Grand Cayman</div></div></div>
<p>The first recorded permanent inhabitant of the Cayman Islands, Isaac Bodden, was born on <a href="/wiki/Grand_Cayman" title="Grand Cayman">Grand Cayman</a> around 1661. He was the grandson of the original settler named Bodden who was probably one of Oliver Cromwell's soldiers at the taking of Jamaica in 1655.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> took <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">formal control</a> of the Cayman Islands, along with Jamaica, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Madrid_(1670)" title="Treaty of Madrid (1670)">Treaty of Madrid of 1670</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> That same year saw an attack on a turtle fishing settlement on Little Cayman by the Spanish under <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Ribeiro_Pardal" title="Manuel Ribeiro Pardal">Manuel Ribeiro Pardal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-keytocayman.com_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-keytocayman.com-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Following several unsuccessful attempts at settlement in what had by now become a haven for pirates,<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> a permanent English-speaking population in the islands dates from the 1730s.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> With settlement, after the first royal land grant by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Jamaica" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor of Jamaica">Governor of Jamaica</a> in 1734, came the perceived need for slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Many were brought to the islands from Africa; this is evident today with the majority of native Caymanians being of African and/or English descent.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>  The results of the first census taken in the islands in 1802 showed the population on Grand Cayman to be 933, with 545 of those inhabitants being enslaved.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Slavery was abolished in the Cayman Islands in 1833. At the time of abolition, there were over 950 blacks of African ancestry enslaved by 116 white families of English ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Cayman_Islands_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Cayman_Islands-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The islands continued to be governed as part of the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Jamaica_(1655%E2%80%931962)" class="mw-redirect" title="Colony of Jamaica (1655–1962)">Colony of Jamaica</a> until 1962, when they became a separate <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown colony</a> while Jamaica became an independent <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heroes_Square_of_George_Town.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Heroes_Square_of_George_Town.jpg/220px-Heroes_Square_of_George_Town.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Heroes_Square_of_George_Town.jpg/330px-Heroes_Square_of_George_Town.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Heroes_Square_of_George_Town.jpg/440px-Heroes_Square_of_George_Town.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1150" data-file-height="738" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heroes_Square_of_George_Town.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Heroes Square in the centre of George Town, which commemorates Cayman Islands' war dead. The Legislative Assembly building is at the left.</div></div></div>
<p>On 8 February 1794, the Caymanians rescued the crews of a group of ten <a href="/wiki/Merchant_ship" title="Merchant ship">merchant ships</a>, including HMS <i>Convert</i>, an incident that has since become known as the <a href="/wiki/Wreck_of_the_Ten_Sail" title="Wreck of the Ten Sail">Wreck of the Ten Sail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Cayman_Islands_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Cayman_Islands-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The ships had struck a reef and run aground during rough seas.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Legend has it that <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="George III of Great Britain and Ireland">King George III</a> rewarded the island with a promise never to introduce taxes as compensation for their generosity, as one of the ships carried a member of the King's own family. While this remains a popular legend, the story is not true.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tourism began to take off in the 1950s with the opening of the airport, a bank and several hotels, plus a number of scheduled flights and cruise stop-overs.<sup id="cite_ref-keytocayman.com_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-keytocayman.com-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Politically the Cayman Islands were an internally self-governing territory of Jamaica from 1958 to 1962, however they reverted to direct British rule following the independence of Jamaica in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> A large degree of internal autonomy was granted by a new constitution in 1972, with further revisions being made in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_10-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The Cayman Islands government focused on boosting the territory's economy via tourism and off-shore finance, both of which mushroomed from the 1970s onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_the_Cayman_Islands-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_10-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The Caymans have historically been a tax-exempt destination, and the government has always relied on indirect and not direct taxes. The territory has never levied <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_gains_tax" title="Capital gains tax">capital gains tax</a>, or any <a href="/wiki/Wealth_tax" title="Wealth tax">wealth tax</a>, making them a popular <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-biswas_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biswas-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The constitution was further modified in 2001 and 2009, codifying various aspects of human rights legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_10-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 September 2004 the island of Grand Cayman, which lies largely unprotected at sea level, was hit by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Hurricane Ivan</a>, creating an 8-ft (2.4&#160;m) <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> which flooded many areas of Grand Cayman.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_10-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>  An estimated 83% of the dwellings on the island were damaged including 4% requiring complete reconstruction. A reported 70% of all dwellings suffered severe damage from flooding or wind. Another 26% sustained minor damage from partial roof removal, low levels of flooding, or impact with floating or wind driven hurricane debris.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Power, water and communications were disrupted for months in some areas as Ivan was the worst hurricane to hit the islands in 86 years.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Grand Cayman began a major rebuilding process and within two years its infrastructure was nearly returned to pre-hurricane status. Due to the tropical location of the islands, more hurricanes or tropical systems have affected the Cayman Islands than any other region in the Atlantic basin; it has been brushed or directly hit, on average, every 2.23 years.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cayman_Islands_Map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cayman_Islands_Map.svg/260px-Cayman_Islands_Map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cayman_Islands_Map.svg/390px-Cayman_Islands_Map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cayman_Islands_Map.svg/520px-Cayman_Islands_Map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="502" data-file-height="249" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cayman_Islands_Map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Cayman Islands, showing the three main islands about 120 kilometres (75 miles) apart</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Geography of the Cayman Islands">Geography of the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<p>The islands are in the western <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> and are the peaks of an <a href="/wiki/Undersea_mountain_range" title="Undersea mountain range">undersea mountain range</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Ridge" title="Cayman Ridge">Cayman Ridge</a> (or Cayman Rise). This ridge flanks the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Trough" title="Cayman Trough">Cayman Trough</a>, 6,000&#160;m (20,000&#160;ft) deep<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> which lies 6&#160;km (3.7&#160;mi) to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The islands lie in the northwest of the Caribbean Sea, east of <a href="/wiki/Quintana_Roo" title="Quintana Roo">Quintana Roo</a>, Mexico and <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yucatán (state)">Yucatán State</a>, Mexico, northeast of Costa Rica, north of Panama, south of Cuba and west of Jamaica. They are situated about 700&#160;km (430&#160;mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami, Florida">Miami</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> 750&#160;km (470&#160;mi) east of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> 366&#160;km (227&#160;mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and about 500&#160;km (310&#160;mi) northwest of <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grand_Cayman" title="Grand Cayman">Grand Cayman</a> is by far the largest, with an area of 197&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (76&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Grand Cayman's two "sister islands", <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Brac" title="Cayman Brac">Cayman Brac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Cayman" title="Little Cayman">Little Cayman</a>, are about 120&#160;km (75&#160;mi) east north-east of Grand Cayman and have areas of 38 and 28.5&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (14.7 and 11.0&#160;sq&#160;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> respectively. The nearest land mass from Grand Cayman is the <a href="/wiki/Canarreos_Archipelago" title="Canarreos Archipelago">Canarreos Archipelago</a> (about 150 miles away), whereas the nearest from the easternmost island Cayman Brac is the <a href="/wiki/Jardines_de_la_Reina" title="Jardines de la Reina">Jardines de la Reina</a> archipelago (about 100 miles away) - both of which are part of Cuba.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterfront,_George_Town,_Grand_Cayman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Waterfront%2C_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg/220px-Waterfront%2C_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Waterfront%2C_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg/330px-Waterfront%2C_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Waterfront%2C_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg/440px-Waterfront%2C_George_Town%2C_Grand_Cayman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterfront,_George_Town,_Grand_Cayman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>George Town waterfront</div></div></div>
<p>All three islands were formed by large <a href="/wiki/Coral_heads" class="mw-redirect" title="Coral heads">coral heads</a> covering submerged ice age peaks of western extensions of the Cuban <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Maestra" title="Sierra Maestra">Sierra Maestra</a> range and are mostly flat. One notable exception to this is <a href="/wiki/The_Bluff_(Cayman_Islands)" title="The Bluff (Cayman Islands)">The Bluff</a> on Cayman Brac's eastern part, which rises to 43&#160;m (141&#160;ft) above sea level, the highest point on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Terrain is mostly a low-lying <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> base surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="List of mammals of the Cayman Islands">List of mammals of the Cayman Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="List of birds of the Cayman Islands">List of birds of the Cayman Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_butterflies_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="List of butterflies of the Cayman Islands">List of butterflies of the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammalian</a> species in the Cayman Islands include the introduced <a href="/wiki/Dasyprocta_punctata" class="mw-redirect" title="Dasyprocta punctata">Central American agouti</a><sup id="cite_ref-MSW3_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSW3-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bats_of_the_Caribbean#Grand_Cayman" class="mw-redirect" title="Bats of the Caribbean">eight species of bats</a>. At least three now extinct <a href="/wiki/List_of_rodents_of_the_Caribbean#Cayman_Islands" title="List of rodents of the Caribbean">native rodent species</a> were present up until the discovery of the islands by Europeans. Marine life around the island of the Grand Cayman includes <a href="/wiki/Tarpon" title="Tarpon">tarpon</a>, silversides (<i><a href="/wiki/Atheriniformes" title="Atheriniformes">Atheriniformes</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/French_angelfish" title="French angelfish">French angelfish</a> (<i>Pomacanthus paru</i>), and <a href="/wiki/Giant_barrel_sponge" title="Giant barrel sponge">giant barrel sponges</a>. A number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_cetacean_species" title="List of cetacean species">cetaceans</a> are found in offshore waters. These species include the <a href="/wiki/Ziphius_cavirostris" class="mw-redirect" title="Ziphius cavirostris">goose-beaked whale</a> (<i>Ziphius cavirostris</i>), <a href="/wiki/Blainville%27s_beaked_whale" title="Blainville&#39;s beaked whale">Blainville's beaked whale</a> (<i>Mesoplodon densirostris</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Sperm_whale" title="Sperm whale">sperm whale</a> (<i>Physeter macrocephalus</i>).
</p><p>Cayman <a href="/wiki/Birds" class="mw-redirect" title="Birds">avian fauna</a> includes two <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> subspecies of <i><a href="/wiki/Amazona" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazona">Amazona</a></i> parrots: <i>Amazona leucocephala hesterna</i> or <a href="/wiki/Cuban_amazon" title="Cuban amazon">Cuban amazon</a>, presently restricted to the island of <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Brac" title="Cayman Brac">Cayman Brac</a>, but formerly also on <a href="/wiki/Little_Cayman" title="Little Cayman">Little Cayman</a>, and <i>Amazona leucocephala caymanensis</i> or <a href="/wiki/Grand_Cayman_parrot" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Cayman parrot">Grand Cayman parrot</a>, which is native to the Cayman Islands, forested areas of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_la_Juventud" title="Isla de la Juventud">Isla de la Juventud</a>. Little Cayman and Cayman Brac are also home to <a href="/wiki/Red-footed_booby" title="Red-footed booby">red-footed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brown_booby" title="Brown booby">brown</a> boobies.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Although the barn owl (<i><a href="/wiki/Tyto_alba" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyto alba">Tyto alba</a></i>) occurs in all three of the islands but they are not commonplace. The Cayman Islands also possess five endemic subspecies of butterflies on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> These butterfly breeds can be viewed at the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II_Botanic_Park" title="Queen Elizabeth II Botanic Park">Queen Elizabeth II Botanic Park</a> on the Grand Cayman.
</p><p>Among other notable fauna at the Queen Elizabeth II Botanic Park is the critically threatened <a href="/wiki/Blue_iguana" title="Blue iguana">blue iguana</a> which is also known as the Grand Cayman iguana (<i>Cyclura lewisi</i>). The blue iguana is endemic to the Grand Cayman<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> particularly because of rocky, sunlit, open areas near the island's shores that are advantageous for the laying of eggs. Nevertheless, habitat destruction and invasive mammalian predators remain primary reasons that blue iguana hatchlings do not survive naturally.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuban_crocodile" title="Cuban crocodile">Cuban crocodile</a> (<i>Crocodylus rhombifer</i>) once inhabited the islands;<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/American_crocodile" title="American crocodile">American crocodile</a> (<i>C. acutus</i>) is thought to be repopulating Grand Cayman. The name "Cayman" is derived from a <a href="/wiki/Cariban_languages" title="Cariban languages">Carib</a> word for various crocodilians.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_signs_rum_point.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Hurricane_signs_rum_point.jpg/220px-Hurricane_signs_rum_point.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Hurricane_signs_rum_point.jpg/330px-Hurricane_signs_rum_point.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Hurricane_signs_rum_point.jpg/440px-Hurricane_signs_rum_point.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2503" data-file-height="2014" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_signs_rum_point.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Signs at Rum Point commemorating landed and near-miss hurricanes</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_the_Cayman_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of the Cayman Islands">Climate of the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<p>The Cayman Islands has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wet_and_dry_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical wet and dry climate">tropical wet and dry climate</a>, with a wet season from May to October, and a dry season that runs from November to April. Seasonally, there is little temperature change.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A major <a href="/wiki/Natural_hazard" title="Natural hazard">natural hazard</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a> that form during the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Atlantic hurricane season">Atlantic hurricane season</a> from June to November.
</p><p>On 11 and 12 September 2004, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Hurricane Ivan</a> struck the Cayman Islands. The storm resulted in two deaths and caused great damage to the infrastructure on the islands. The total economic impact of the storms was estimated to be $3.4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Demographics of the Cayman Islands">Demographics of the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<p>According to the Economics and Statistics Office of the Government of the Cayman Islands, the Cayman Islands has a population of about 64,420 as of spring 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-eso_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eso-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The Cayman Islands has more registered businesses than people.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the Cayman Islands had an estimated population of about 60,765 according to the United Nations,<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> representing a mix of more than 100 nationalities. Of that number, about half are of Caymanian descent. About 60 percent of the population is of mixed race (mostly mixed African-European). <a href="/wiki/White_Caribbeans" title="White Caribbeans">Whites</a> make up 20 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The islands are almost exclusively Christian, with large numbers of Baptists, Presbyterians and Catholics, but also host Jewish,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Muslim and Hindu communities. The majority of the population resides on <a href="/wiki/Grand_Cayman" title="Grand Cayman">Grand Cayman</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Brac" title="Cayman Brac">Cayman Brac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Cayman" title="Little Cayman">Little Cayman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The capital of the Cayman Islands is <a href="/wiki/George_Town,_Cayman_Islands" title="George Town, Cayman Islands">George Town</a>, on the southwest coast of Grand Cayman.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="District_populations">District populations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: District populations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_caymanian_home_east_end.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Traditional_caymanian_home_east_end.jpg/220px-Traditional_caymanian_home_east_end.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Traditional_caymanian_home_east_end.jpg/330px-Traditional_caymanian_home_east_end.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Traditional_caymanian_home_east_end.jpg/440px-Traditional_caymanian_home_east_end.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2337" data-file-height="1559" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_caymanian_home_east_end.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional Caymanian home at East End, Grand Cayman</div></div></div>
<p>According to the Cayman Islands 2016 Compendium of Statistics released by the Economics and Statistics Office (ESO) the estimated resident population is above 61,000 people,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> broken down as follows:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/George_Town,_Cayman_Islands" title="George Town, Cayman Islands">George Town</a>: 31,935</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Bay,_Cayman_Islands" title="West Bay, Cayman Islands">West Bay</a>: 11,686</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bodden_Town_(village)" title="Bodden Town (village)">Bodden Town</a>: 12,669</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/North_Side,_Cayman_Islands" title="North Side, Cayman Islands">North Side</a>: 1,460</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/East_End,_Cayman_Islands" title="East End, Cayman Islands">East End</a>: 1,511</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cayman_Brac" title="Cayman Brac">Cayman Brac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Cayman" title="Little Cayman">Little Cayman</a> (Sister Islands): 2,099</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Cayman_Islands.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Tree_map_export_2009_Cayman_Islands.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cayman_Islands.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Tree_map_export_2009_Cayman_Islands.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cayman_Islands.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Tree_map_export_2009_Cayman_Islands.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cayman_Islands.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1104" data-file-height="862" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Cayman_Islands.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphical depiction of the Cayman Islands' product exports</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Economy of the Cayman Islands">Economy of the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<p>With an average income of around KYD$47,000, Caymanians have the highest standard of living in the Caribbean. According to the <a href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a>, the Cayman Islands GDP per capita is the 38th highest in the world, but the CIA's data for Cayman dates to 2004 and is likely to be lower than present-day values.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The territory prints its own currency, the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands_dollar" title="Cayman Islands dollar">Cayman Islands dollar</a> (KYD), which is pegged to the <a href="/wiki/US_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="US dollar">US dollar</a> US$1.227 to 1 KYD. However, in many retail stores throughout the islands, the KYD is typically traded at US$1.25.<sup id="cite_ref-Cayman_Currency_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cayman_Currency-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The government has established a <a href="/wiki/Needs_Assessment_Unit" title="Needs Assessment Unit">Needs Assessment Unit</a> to relieve poverty in the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, the Cayman Islands holds a relatively low unemployment rate of about 4.24% as of 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> lower than the value of 4.7% that was recorded in 2014.
</p><p>The government's primary source of income is <a href="/wiki/Indirect_tax" title="Indirect tax">indirect taxation</a>: there is no <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_gains_tax" title="Capital gains tax">capital gains tax</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Corporation_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporation tax">corporation tax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-biswas_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biswas-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Import_duty" class="mw-redirect" title="Import duty">import duty</a> of 5% to 22% (automobiles 29.5% to 100%) is levied against goods imported into the islands. Few goods are exempt; notable exemptions include books, cameras, gold, and perfume.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 July 2012 one of the Cayman Islands' former Premiers <a href="/wiki/McKeeva_Bush" title="McKeeva Bush">McKeeva Bush</a> announced the intended introduction of a "community enhancement fee" in the form of a <a href="/wiki/Payroll_tax" title="Payroll tax">payroll tax</a> to be paid solely by expatriate workers. Caymanians themselves were to remain exempt from this tax. This would have been the first direct tax on income in the Cayman Islands' history.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Bush also announced a five percent fee on "certain categories of employment" to be payable by businesses. However, the payroll tax was scrapped before it had been implemented.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving_in_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Scuba diving in the Cayman Islands">Scuba diving in the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1408px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Seven_Mile_Beach_2006.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of Seven Mile Beach on Grand Cayman."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Seven_Mile_Beach_2006.jpg/1400px-Seven_Mile_Beach_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="1400" height="115" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Seven_Mile_Beach_2006.jpg/2100px-Seven_Mile_Beach_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Seven_Mile_Beach_2006.jpg/2800px-Seven_Mile_Beach_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="11744" data-file-height="968" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seven_Mile_Beach_2006.jpg" title="File:Seven Mile Beach 2006.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/Panorama" title="Panorama">Panorama</a> of <a href="/wiki/Seven_Mile_Beach,_Grand_Cayman" title="Seven Mile Beach, Grand Cayman">Seven Mile Beach</a> on <a href="/wiki/Grand_Cayman" title="Grand Cayman">Grand Cayman</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>One of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Cayman" title="Grand Cayman">Grand Cayman</a>'s main attractions is <a href="/wiki/Seven_Mile_Beach,_Grand_Cayman" title="Seven Mile Beach, Grand Cayman">Seven Mile Beach</a>, site of a number of the island's hotels and resorts. Named one of the Ultimate Beaches by Caribbean Travel and Life, Seven Mile Beach is a public beach on the western shore of Grand Cayman Island.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Historical sites in Grand Cayman, such as <a href="/wiki/Pedro_St._James_Castle" title="Pedro St. James Castle">Pedro St. James Castle</a> in Savannah, also attract visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stingraypassing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fe/Stingraypassing.jpg/220px-Stingraypassing.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fe/Stingraypassing.jpg/330px-Stingraypassing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fe/Stingraypassing.jpg/440px-Stingraypassing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2907" data-file-height="2180" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stingraypassing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stingray passing through – <a href="/wiki/Stingray_City,_Grand_Cayman" title="Stingray City, Grand Cayman">Stingray City, Grand Cayman</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Southern_Stingrays_At_Stingray_City_Grand_Cayman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Southern_Stingrays_At_Stingray_City_Grand_Cayman.jpg/220px-Southern_Stingrays_At_Stingray_City_Grand_Cayman.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Southern_Stingrays_At_Stingray_City_Grand_Cayman.jpg/330px-Southern_Stingrays_At_Stingray_City_Grand_Cayman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Southern_Stingrays_At_Stingray_City_Grand_Cayman.jpg/440px-Southern_Stingrays_At_Stingray_City_Grand_Cayman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1145" data-file-height="644" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Southern_Stingrays_At_Stingray_City_Grand_Cayman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stingrays pass each other at Stingray City sandbar off Grand Cayman Island</div></div></div>
<p>All three islands offer <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a>, and the Cayman Islands is home to several snorkelling locations where tourists can swim with <a href="/wiki/Stingray" title="Stingray">stingrays</a>. The most popular area to do this is <a href="/wiki/Stingray_City,_Grand_Cayman" title="Stingray City, Grand Cayman">Stingray City, Grand Cayman</a>. Stingray City is a top attraction in Grand Cayman and originally started in the 1980s, when divers started feeding squid to stingrays. The stingrays started to associate the sound of the boat motors with food, and thus visit this area year round.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are two <a href="/wiki/Shipwreck" title="Shipwreck">shipwrecks</a> off the shores of Cayman Brac, including the <a href="/wiki/Sinking_ships_for_wreck_diving_sites#List_of_ships_sunk_for_wreck_diving" title="Sinking ships for wreck diving sites">MV Captain Keith Tibbetts</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Grand Cayman also has several shipwrecks off its shores, including one deliberate one. On 30 September 1994 the <a href="/wiki/USS_Kittiwake_(ASR-13)" title="USS Kittiwake (ASR-13)">USS&#160;<i>Kittiwake</i></a> was decommissioned and struck from the Naval Vessel Register. In November 2008 her ownership was transferred for an undisclosed amount to the government of the Cayman Islands, which had decided to sink the <i>Kittiwake</i> in June 2009 to form a new artificial reef off Seven Mile Beach, Grand Cayman. Following several delays, the ship was finally scuttled according to plan on 5 January 2011. The <i>Kittiwake</i> has become a dynamic environment for marine life. While visitors are not allowed to take anything, there are endless sights. Each of the five decks of the ship offers squirrelfish, rare sponges, Goliath groupers, urchins, and more. Experienced and beginner divers are invited to swim around the <i>Kittiwake</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <span id="Pirates_Week"></span> Pirates Week is an annual 11-day November festival started in 1977 by then-Minister of Tourism Jim Bodden to boost tourism during the country's tourism slow season.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other Grand Cayman tourist attractions include: the ironshore landscape of <a href="/wiki/Hell,_Grand_Cayman" title="Hell, Grand Cayman">Hell</a>; the 23-acre (93,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) marine theme park "<a href="/wiki/Cayman_Turtle_Centre" title="Cayman Turtle Centre">Cayman Turtle Centre</a>: Island Wildlife Encounter", previously known as "Boatswain's Beach"; the production of gourmet <a href="/wiki/Sea_salt" title="Sea salt">sea salt</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Mastic_Reserve" title="Mastic Reserve">Mastic Trail</a>, a hiking trail through the forests in the centre of the island. The National Trust for the Cayman Islands provides guided tours weekly on the Mastic Trail and other locations.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another attraction to visit on Grand Cayman is the Observation Tower, located in Camana Bay. The Observation Tower is 75 feet tall and provides 360-degree views across Seven Mile Beach, George Town, the North Sound, and beyond. It is free to the public and climbing the tower has become a popular thing to do in the Cayman Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Points of interest include the <a href="/wiki/East_End_Light" title="East End Light">East End Light</a> (sometimes called Gorling Bluff Light), a lighthouse at the east end of Grand Cayman island. The lighthouse is the centrepiece of East End Lighthouse Park, managed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_the_Cayman_Islands" title="National Trust for the Cayman Islands">National Trust for the Cayman Islands</a>; the first navigational aid on the site was the first lighthouse in the Cayman Islands.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shipping">Shipping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Shipping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 31&#160;December&#160;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> 360 commercial vessels and 1,674 pleasure craft were registered in the Cayman Islands totaling 4.3 million <a href="/wiki/Gross_tonnage" title="Gross tonnage">GT</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labour">Labour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Labour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamaican_woodcarver_Bodden_Town_Grand_Cayman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jamaican_woodcarver_Bodden_Town_Grand_Cayman.jpg/220px-Jamaican_woodcarver_Bodden_Town_Grand_Cayman.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jamaican_woodcarver_Bodden_Town_Grand_Cayman.jpg/330px-Jamaican_woodcarver_Bodden_Town_Grand_Cayman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jamaican_woodcarver_Bodden_Town_Grand_Cayman.jpg/440px-Jamaican_woodcarver_Bodden_Town_Grand_Cayman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2196" data-file-height="1456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamaican_woodcarver_Bodden_Town_Grand_Cayman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jamaican-born roadside woodcarver working outside <a href="/wiki/Bodden_Town_(village)" title="Bodden Town (village)">Bodden Town</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Cayman Islands has a small population of 64,420 (as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>) and therefore a limited workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-eso_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eso-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Work_permit" title="Work permit">Work permits</a> may, therefore, be granted to foreigners. On average, there have been more than 21,000 foreigners holding valid work permits.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Work_permits_for_non-citizens">Work permits for non-citizens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Work permits for non-citizens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>To work in the Cayman Islands as a <a href="/wiki/Alien_(law)" title="Alien (law)">non-citizen</a>, a work permit is required. This involves passing a police background check and a health check. A prospective immigrant worker will not be granted a permit unless certain medical conditions are met, including testing negative for <a href="/wiki/Syphilis" title="Syphilis">syphilis</a> and <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>. A permit may be granted to individuals on special work.
</p><p>A foreigner must first have a job to move to the Cayman Islands. The employer applies and pays for the work permit.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Work permits are not granted to foreigners who are in the Cayman Islands (unless it is a renewal). The Cayman Islands Immigration Department requires foreigners to remain out of the country until their work permit has been approved.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Cayman Islands presently imposes a controversial "rollover" in relation to <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriate</a> workers who require a work permit. Non-Caymanians are only permitted to reside and work within the territory for a maximum of nine years unless they satisfy the criteria of key employees. Non-Caymanians who are "rolled over" may return to work additional nine-year periods, subject to a one-year gap between their periods of work. The policy has been the subject of some controversy within the press. Law firms have been particularly upset by the recruitment difficulties that it has caused.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Other less well-remunerated employment sectors have been affected as well. Concerns about safety have been expressed by diving instructors, and realtors have also expressed concerns. Others support the rollover as necessary to protect Caymanian identity in the face of immigration of large numbers of expatriate workers.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Concerns have been expressed that in the long term, the policy may damage the preeminence of the Cayman Islands as an <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">offshore financial centre</a> by making it difficult to recruit and retain experienced staff from onshore financial centres. Government employees are no longer exempt from this "rollover" policy, according to this report in a local newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The governor has used his constitutional powers, which give him absolute control over the disposition of <a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">civil service</a> employees, to determine which expatriate civil servants are dismissed after seven years service and which are not.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>This policy is incorporated in the Immigration Law (2003 revision), written by the United Democratic Party government, and subsequently enforced by the People's Progressive Movement Party government. Both governments agree to the term limits on foreign workers, and the majority of Caymanians also agree it is necessary to protect local culture and heritage from being eroded by a large number of foreigners gaining residency and citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="CARICOM_Single_Market_Economy">CARICOM Single Market Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: CARICOM Single Market Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In recognition of the CARICOM (Free Movement) Skilled Persons Act which came into effect in July 1997 in some of the CARICOM countries such as Jamaica and which has been adopted in other CARICOM countries, such as Trinidad and Tobago<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> it is possible that CARICOM nationals who hold the "A Certificate of Recognition of Caribbean Community Skilled Person" may be allowed to work in the Cayman Islands<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> under normal working conditions.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Politics of the Cayman Islands">Politics of the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cayman_islands_legislative_assembly.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/Cayman_islands_legislative_assembly.JPG/170px-Cayman_islands_legislative_assembly.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/Cayman_islands_legislative_assembly.JPG/255px-Cayman_islands_legislative_assembly.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/Cayman_islands_legislative_assembly.JPG/340px-Cayman_islands_legislative_assembly.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cayman_islands_legislative_assembly.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Legislative Assembly building in <a href="/wiki/George_Town,_Cayman_Islands" title="George Town, Cayman Islands">George Town</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" data-file-width="2206" data-file-height="1358" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the European Union in the world with <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">overseas countries and territories and outermost regions</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Cayman Islands is a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British overseas territory</a>, listed by the UN Special Committee of 24 as one of the 16 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">non-self-governing territories</a>. The current Constitution, incorporating a Bill of Rights, was ordained by a <a href="/wiki/Statutory_Instrument_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Statutory Instrument (UK)">statutory instrument</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> A 19-seat (not including two non-voting members appointed by the Governor which brings the total to 21 members) <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Legislative Assembly of the Cayman Islands">Legislative Assembly</a> is elected by the people every four years to handle domestic affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Of the elected Members of the Legislative Assembly (MLAs), seven are chosen to serve as government Ministers in a Cabinet headed by the Governor. The <a href="/wiki/Premier" title="Premier">Premier</a> is appointed by the Governor.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Governor of the Cayman Islands">Governor</a> is appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">Queen</a> of the United Kingdom on the advice of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">British Government</a> to represent the monarch.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Governors can exercise complete legislative and executive authority if they wish through blanket powers reserved to them in the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Bills which have passed the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative Assembly">Legislative Assembly</a> require <a href="/wiki/Royal_assent" title="Royal assent">royal assent</a> before becoming effective. The Constitution empowers the Governor to withhold <a href="/wiki/Royal_assent" title="Royal assent">royal assent</a> in cases where the legislation appears to him or her to be repugnant to or inconsistent with the Constitution or affects the rights and privileges of the Legislative Assembly or the Royal Prerogative, or matters reserved to the Governor by article 55.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The executive authority of the Cayman Islands is vested in <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">the Queen</a> and is exercised by the Government, consisting of the Governor and the Cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> There is an office of the Deputy Governor, who must be a Caymanian and have served in a senior public office. The Deputy Governor is the acting Governor when the office of Governor is vacant, or the Governor is not able to discharge his or her duties or is absent from the Cayman Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The current Governor of the Cayman Islands is <a href="/wiki/Martyn_Roper" title="Martyn Roper">Martyn Roper</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Cabinet is composed of two official members and seven elected members, called Ministers; one of whom is designated <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Premier of the Cayman Islands">Premier</a>. The Premier can serve for two consecutive terms after which he or she is barred from attaining the office again. Although an MLA can only be Premier twice any person who meets the qualifications and requirements for a seat in the Legislative Assembly can be elected to the Legislative Assembly indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are two official members of the Legislative Assembly, the <a href="/wiki/Deputy_governor" title="Deputy governor">Deputy Governor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Attorney_general" title="Attorney general">Attorney General</a>. They are appointed by the Governor in accordance with Her Majesty's instructions, and although they have seats in the Legislative Assembly, under the 2009 Constitution, they do not vote. They serve in a professional and advisory role to the MLAs, the Deputy Governor represents the Governor who is a representative of the Queen and the British Government. While the Attorney General serves to advise on legal matters and has special responsibilities in the LA, he is generally responsible for changes to the Penal code among other things.
</p><p>The seven Ministers are voted into office by the 19 elected members of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Legislative Assembly of the Cayman Islands">Legislative Assembly of the Cayman Islands</a>. One of the Ministers, the leader of the majority political party, is appointed Premier by the Governor.
</p><p>After consulting the Premier, the Governor allocates a portfolio of responsibilities to each Cabinet Minister. Under the principle of collective responsibility, all Ministers are obliged to support in the Assembly any measures approved by Cabinet.
</p><p>Almost 80 departments, sections and units carry out the business of government, joined by a number of statutory boards and authorities set up for specific purposes, such as the Port Authority, the Civil Aviation Authority, the Immigration Board, the Water Authority, the University College Board of Governors, the National Pensions Board and the Health Insurance Commission.
</p><p>Since 2000, there have been two official major political parties: The <a href="/wiki/United_Democratic_Party_(Cayman_Islands)" class="mw-redirect" title="United Democratic Party (Cayman Islands)">Cayman Democratic Party</a> (CDP) and the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Progressive_Movement_(Cayman_Islands)" title="People&#39;s Progressive Movement (Cayman Islands)">People's Progressive Movement</a> (PPM). While there has been a shift to political parties, many contending for office still run as independents. The two parties are notably similar, though they consider each other rivals in most cases, their differences are generally in personality and implementation rather than actual policy. The Cayman Islands currently lacks any real liberal or progressive representation in the Legislative Assembly or in the form of organized political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> As of the May 2017 General Election, members of the PPM and CDP have joined together with 3 independent members to form a government coalition despite many years of enmity.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defence_and_law_enforcement">Defence and law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Defence and law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The defence of the Cayman Islands is the responsibility of the United Kingdom. Law enforcement in the country is provided chiefly by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Cayman_Islands_Police_Service" title="Royal Cayman Islands Police Service">Royal Cayman Islands Police Service</a> and the Cayman Islands Customs Department. These two agencies co-operate in aspects of law enforcement, including their <a href="/wiki/Royal_Cayman_Islands_Police_Service#Joint_Marine_Unit" title="Royal Cayman Islands Police Service">joint marine unit</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands_Cadet_Corps" title="Cayman Islands Cadet Corps">Cayman Islands Cadet Corps</a> was formed in March 2001 and carries out military-type training with teenage citizens of the country. As of 2017 the PPM led Coalition government have pledged to form a Coast Guard to protect the interests of the Islands, especially in terms of illegal immigration and illegal drug importation.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>No direct taxation is imposed on residents and Cayman Islands companies. The government receives the majority of its income from indirect taxation. Duty is levied against most imported goods, which is typically in the range of 22% to 25%. Some items are exempted, such as baby formula, books, cameras and certain items are taxed at 5%. Duty on automobiles depends on their value. The duty can amount to 29.5% up to $20,000.00 KYD CIF (cost, insurance and freight) and up to 42% over $30,000.00 KYD CIF for expensive models. The government charges flat licensing fees on financial institutions that operate in the islands and there are work permit fees on foreign labour. A 13% government tax is placed on all tourist accommodations in addition to US$37.50 airport departure tax which is built into the cost of an airline ticket. There are no taxes on corporate profits, capital gains, or personal income. There are no estate or death inheritance taxes payable on Cayman Islands real estate or other assets held in the Cayman Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Foreign relations of the Cayman Islands">Foreign relations of the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1953caymanislands1poundelizabethIIblue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/1953caymanislands1poundelizabethIIblue.jpg/140px-1953caymanislands1poundelizabethIIblue.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/1953caymanislands1poundelizabethIIblue.jpg/210px-1953caymanislands1poundelizabethIIblue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/1953caymanislands1poundelizabethIIblue.jpg/280px-1953caymanislands1poundelizabethIIblue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="318" data-file-height="467" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1953caymanislands1poundelizabethIIblue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Postage stamp with portrait of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, 1953</div></div></div>
<p>Foreign policy is controlled by the United Kingdom, as the islands remain an overseas territory of the United Kingdom. Although in its early days, the Cayman Islands' most important relationships were with Britain and <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, in recent years, as a result of economic dependence, a relationship with the United States has developed.
</p><p>Though the Cayman Islands is involved in no major international disputes, they have come under some criticism due to the use of their territory for narcotics trafficking and <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a>. In an attempt to address this, the government entered into the Narcotics Agreement of 1984 and the <a href="/wiki/Mutual_Legal_Assistance_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutual Legal Assistance Treaty">Mutual Legal Assistance Treaty</a> of 1986 with the United States, to reduce the use of their facilities associated with these activities. In more recent years, they have stepped up the fight against money laundering, by limiting banking secrecy, introducing requirements for customer identification and record keeping, and requiring banks to co-operate with foreign investigators.
</p><p>Due to their status as an overseas territory of the UK, the Cayman Islands has no representation either in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> or in most other international organisations. However, the Cayman Islands still participates in some international organisations, being an associate member of <a href="/wiki/Caricom" class="mw-redirect" title="Caricom">Caricom</a> and <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, and a member of a sub-bureau of <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">Interpol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Transport in the Cayman Islands">Transport in the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ports">Ports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>George Town is the port capital of Grand Cayman. There are no berthing facilities for cruise ships, but up to four cruise ships can anchor in designated anchorages. There are three cruise terminals in George Town, the North, South, and Royal Watler Terminals. The ride from the ship to the terminal is about 5 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Air transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_Cayman_Islands" title="List of airports in the Cayman Islands">List of airports in the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Cayman_Islands" title="Education in the Cayman Islands">Education in the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_schools">Primary and secondary schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayman_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_the_Cayman_Islands" title="List of schools in the Cayman Islands">List of schools in the Cayman Islands</a></div>
<p>The Cayman Islands Education Department operates state schools. Caymanian children are entitled to free primary and secondary education. There are two public high schools on Grand Cayman, <a href="/wiki/John_Gray_High_School" title="John Gray High School">John Gray High School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clifton_Hunter_High_School" title="Clifton Hunter High School">Clifton Hunter High School</a>, and one on Cayman Brac, <a href="/wiki/Layman_E._Scott_High_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Layman E.
